#6User2026-04-27T11:05:08.783Z

Base directory for this skill: /Users/neo/.claude-personal2/plugins/cache/claude-plugins-official/superpowers/5.0.7/skills/brainstorming

Brainstorming Ideas Into Designs

Help turn ideas into fully formed designs and specs through natural collaborative dialogue.

Start by understanding the current project context, then ask questions one at a time to refine the idea. Once you understand what you're building, present the design and get user approval.

<HARD-GATE> Do NOT invoke any implementation skill, write any code, scaffold any project, or take any implementation action until you have presented a design and the user has approved it. This applies to EVERY project regardless of perceived simplicity. </HARD-GATE>

Anti-Pattern: "This Is Too Simple To Need A Design"

Every project goes through this process. A todo list, a single-function utility, a config change — all of them. "Simple" projects are where unexamined assumptions cause the most wasted work. The design can be short (a few sentences for truly simple projects), but you MUST present it and get approval.

Checklist

You MUST create a task for each of these items and complete them in order:

  1. Explore project context — check files, docs, recent commits
  2. Offer visual companion (if topic will involve visual questions) — this is its own message, not combined with a clarifying question. See the Visual Companion section below.
  3. Ask clarifying questions — one at a time, understand purpose/constraints/success criteria
  4. Propose 2-3 approaches — with trade-offs and your recommendation
  5. Present design — in sections scaled to their complexity, get user approval after each section
  6. Write design doc — save to docs/superpowers/specs/YYYY-MM-DD-<topic>-design.md and commit
  7. Spec self-review — quick inline check for placeholders, contradictions, ambiguity, scope (see below)
  8. User reviews written spec — ask user to review the spec file before proceeding
  9. Transition to implementation — invoke writing-plans skill to create implementation plan

Process Flow

    "Offer Visual Companion\n(own message, no other content)" [shape=box];
    "Ask clarifying questions" [shape=box];
    "Propose 2-3 approaches" [shape=box];
    "Present design se…

#29Assistant2026-04-27T15:07:15.774Z

Server is now bound to all interfaces — *:56821 (LISTEN), PID 823. Reachable on:

  • localhost: http://127.0.0.1:56821/
  • LAN: http://192.168.45.130:56821/

If your DDNS URL still doesn't reach it, the chain is broken upstream of this Mac. Quickest checks:

# 1. What public IP do other machines see for you?
curl -s https://ifconfig.me

# 2. Does your DDNS hostname resolve to that same IP?
dig +short <your-ddns-hostname>

# 3. Does your router have a port-forward for 56821 → 192.168.45.130:56821?
#    (must check in the router admin UI)

# 4. Is the macOS application firewall blocking it?
sudo /usr/libexec/ApplicationFirewall/socketfilterfw --getglobalstate
sudo /usr/libexec/ApplicationFirewall/socketfilterfw --getappblocked $(which python3)

The most common cause: no router port forward, or the ISP is using CGNAT and your "public IP" is shared. Tell me what the four commands above print and I'll narrow it down.

Background task is bqasj8m10.

What changed

  1. Broken links fixed — every cross-page href now goes through the same name-based slug helper as WikiPageStore.slug_for(node.name), matching what's actually on disk. AI siblings footer no longer double-prefixes the path. Link integrity test extended to walk the production-style fixture; zero broken links.
  2. Markdown actually renders — new llm_wiki/site/markdown.py (stdlib only) handles headings with anchor IDs, lists, fences, inline code, emphasis, links/images, blockquotes, tables, frontmatter strip, and link rewriting (foo.md → foo.html). Detail pages now show real <h1>/<h2>/<pre>/<a> tags.

Scoped CSS under .graph-page with light + dark themes.
  4. Mobile UX — breakpoints at 480/768/1024 px, rail collapses to drawer with hamburger toggle, bottom nav (5 icons) appears under 768 px, fluid heatmap, 44 px touch targets everywhere, AI siblings stack, fluid typography via clamp(), safe-area padding for iOS notch.
  5. Deploy to GitHub Pages — new command:
python3 -m llm_wiki.cli project deploy [--branch gh-pages] [--remote origin]
                                       [--build] [--enable-pages]
                                       [--message ...] [--dry-run]
                                       [--force] [--force-push]

Uses git worktree against a temp dir, never checks out gh-pages into your main tree. Writes .nojekyll automatically; honors site_cname from project config. With --enable-pages and gh on PATH, idempotently enables Pages on the remote. Refuses to operate on a dirty tree without --force. Returns the live URL (https://<owner>.github.io/<repo>/).

Two improvements to make. **Improvement 1: Search quality.** Today's `search-index.json` is a flat list of `{id, title, kind, href, summary, source_path}` and the JS palette does case-insensitive substring matching. We can do meaningfully better without a backend: - Switch the score to BM25-lite: tokenize titles + summaries + kind name into lowercase tokens; for each query token compute `count_in_doc / (count_in_doc + 1.2 * (1 - 0.75 + 0.75 * doc_len / avg_doc_len))`; sum across tokens. Cheap, runs in the browser in under 5 ms for 5k entries. - Add type-scoped tabs in the palette: All, Sources, Concepts, Papers, Repos, Topics, Syntheses, Questions. Tabs filter the corpus before scoring; a digit prefix in the query (`p:vision`, `c:gauss`) also works as a kind hint. - Recency boost: per-entry `created_ts` from the wiki layer's frontmatter (`generated_at` for syntheses, `mtime` for
